  115. Works pretty well! I did have some problems using it at first, so I'm going to share some tips with you. 1) Wipe everything down with pure acetone, or use a nail polish remover that does NOT contain any oils. The first one I used had a moisturizer in it, and the polish would not stick well to the stamper 2) Slightly rough your stamper up with a fine grit nail file. This will help pick up the polish from the plates 3) The metal scraper will scratch your plates. You don't need to press down hard, just be sure to hold it at a 45 degree angle 4) Work FAST. I was taking my dear sweet time and the polish dries and then won't stick to the stamper or your nail 5) Be sure to put down a base coat (clear or colored) first. Stamping directly to my nails doesn't work so well 6) You can use ANY polish you want. It doesn't have to be the Konad \\"special polish\\". However, thinner polishes won't show up well. So if you're going to use a white or a lighter color, older or goopy polishes work better. 7) The plates from BUNDLE MONSTER are great! You get 20-some plates with 4-8 designs on them and they're lots of fun. Some of the plates compliment each other and are great for layering multiple colors. [[ASIN:B003ILUQPM Bundle Monster Nail Art 21pc Stamping Plates]] or [[ASIN:B004XJNQXW Bundle Monster Nail Art Nailart 25pc Stamping Plates]] Hope this helps everyone out there. ENJOY! ~MJ!~

I gave up and ordered the Konad online and waited for it to come. When it came I tried it again and still nothing! So I knew for sure it was me that was doing something wrong.<br /><br />What no one tells you online is that you have to press lightly onto the stamp for the color to transfer. Then press firmly when applying it to your nails. Each with a side rolling motion. Start from one side and roll to the other.<br /><br />I'm still working on the technique, but now that I get how to do it it's just a matter of time before I'm a pro at this. :-)<br /><br />So remember everyone press lightly to get the design off the stamp and press firmly to press onto the nail.<br /><br />Have fun and Enjoy!!!

  448. I've had this for over 6 months and I honestly can't ask for anything else considering I got exactly what I paid for. What came in the mail was a genuine Konad stamper. I was scared to purchase this and have it be a knock-off but I got the real deal. I ordered this stamper with a set of 25 stamping plates and all my friends are wondering how I got such perfect designs on my nails! For those of you who are having trouble with the scraper not scraping very well... you need to buy stamping polish! Stamping polish is MUCH more thick and sticky than regular polish. You do not need to glob it onto the entire design on the plate, but only a thick strip on the side of the design and when you scrape it, the scraper should spread it over the plate design (I hope that makes sense). This will avoid streaks and frustration!! Of course, you can use regular polish to stamp with, but it will not be as opaque. Some formulas are thicker than others, my best suggestion for a dupe of Konad Stamping Polish is &#34;Sally Hansen Insta Dri WHIRLWIND WHITE&#34; for the white polish and &#34;Rimmel Black Satin&#34; for the black polish. I got these dupe suggestions from a famous nail-tutorial youtuber (elleandish) and they are pretty good replacements if you don't wanna spend the extra money. Another tip would be to ROLL on the design (when picking up the design from the plate and also when putting the design on your nails). ROLL ROLL ROLL ROLL ROLL!!!! Also, you want to be QUICK when stamping your nails as you do not want the design to DRY on the stamper! Hope you guys have fun with your Stamper and Scraper, I really do recommend it!

  472. Okay, first off: I am guilty of loving my stamping plates a whole lot. The scraper is fine to work with, although, the small grooves and holes in it collect nailpolish and need to be cleaned off every few swipes. IMO, an expired giftcard works just as well and is easier to clean off.<br /><br />Unfortunately, there are no cheap substitutes for the stamper. I suggest you guard it with your life. It is flexible and can mold itself onto the nail to ensure a proper image stamp. The double ended one is perfect for making small adjustment to the nail (eg: the plate image is too small to cover the entire nail) and you have to make a second 'swipe'. The stamp end is about 1\\" round. It cleans up beautifully with Acetone and after hundreds of cleanings, still looks new.<br /><br />Just an FYI, as I've been Konad'ing for a bit now, instead of the black \\"Konad Special Polish\\", I have found (after trying 11 different products) that WET 'N WILD black velvet nailpolish is the best. It costs less than $2 at CVS or WalMart and it is by far the best black out there. I've tried Orly, Chanel, and others, and none of them are this thick and black. Others are too sheer when you try to stamp them, or they simply don't show up on a darker background. I like to do dark blue with a black argyle pattern on them. Looks great, just don't forget your topcoat.<br /><br />Now, for the regular stamping polishes... what I have found is that any basecoat color is fine. Its when you need one to stamp with that you have to be careful. Don't be fooled by others who say that 'any nailpolish will stamp'. Well, yes it will, but it may be so faint that it will be a waste of your time. The best nailpolishes for stamping are ones that have some metallic in them. Sally Hansen Chrome nailpens are good, but expensive. I have found that the best stamping polishes are at WalMart. Yes, PURE ICE nailpolishs in 'Outrageous' and others stamp up beautifully. They are thick, quick drying and accurate. I only use the ones with a bit of 'chrome-iness\\" to them. If you're going to put a design on your nail, make it pop!<br /><br />For the White polish, Sally Hansen French Tip White is a good one. White is tricky. It almost has to be like 'liquid paper' to get it to work and look right.<br /><br />Good luck, fellow nail afficiandos!. I only use the ones with a bit of 'chrome-iness\\" to them. If you're going to put a design on your nail, make it pop!<br /><br />For the White polish, Sally Hansen French Tip White is a good one. White is tricky. It almost has to be like 'liquid paper' to get it to work and look right.<br /><br />Good luck, fellow nail afficiandos!

  714. I got this, the 25 plate kit and the Konad black and white polishes. They work great!<br /><br />SOME THINGS I LEARNED:<br /><br />-You really need to buy the special Konad polish, it is different than regular nail polish.<br />-Always shake the bottle of Konad Polish VERY well before you use it, otherwise it will not stick to the pad like it should.<br />-You can use the plate on no more than 2 or 3 nails before you need to clean it and the scraper off with nail polish remover, then continue.<br />-Some plates are not quite big enough to cover your nail, just add polish to a portion of the plate and use that to add more of the pattern.<br />-It takes a bit of practice, but by my second hand it was a lot easier!<br />-It helps a lot to have one of the manicure clean-up pens for your cuticles (full of nail polish remover) because some of the pattern will stick to your skin. It does come off really easily though.<br /><br />Have fun with this! I know I am!

  716. It took me several trials & mistakes to figure out how this thing works. Once figured, like others said, it was fast and easy. I got this thing with french manicure image plate and I'm very pleased with how my nails look!! I wish I knew about this product earlier. I really like that I don't have to wait for it to dry forever like I would when painting the tip. Whoever came up with this idea of stamping a nail polish is just brilliant!!! If you are new to Konading, here are the two sites that really helped me get started on Konadicure :) -Regular polishes that work for Konadicure: [...] My absolute favorite konading polishes are Sally Hansen Insta-Dri :) -No, you really DON'T need to cover the whole image and waste your nail polish(es)!!: [...] My only complain is that the scraper could have been better designed, not that it doesn't work, but the metal scratch up the image plates and it is not very easy to clean; the polish gets inside the holes and between the thin ridges of the blade. So I listened to others and used my expired bank card. I cut it in half for better grip and it worked!!! It is way easier to clean up; I just smear what's scraped on to paper towel or old T-shirt. The only thing you have to make sure is that your card isn't chipped, make sure its smooth and straight. Another thing I found out is: you can use plastic tapes to clean up most of the image that got onto your finger instead of using nail polish remover as long as you are using regular nail polishes. I heard acetone gets absorbed into your skin very quickly and that is just no good for your finger nor cuticle, so it's best to avoid if you don't have to. Just be careful not to put tape onto the image you just stamped. For this, I make a ring of tape and have it available before I stamping. This cleaning method also works for cleaning up the stamper with leftover image; I just stamp the stamper on a larger ring of tape stuck on my work area and I don't have to worry about lint getting on the rubber part from using cotton balls or Q tips. Overall, I'm very happy with this product and I will definitely buy again if mine breaks though I can't see how such a simple thing can break. The rubber tip might come off, but all you need is a crazy glue...

  839. I like the quality of this stamper, and I did receive a Konad brand, I'm not sure why others did not. As others suggested here I used an old store card instead of the metal scraper, I've never used it as the idea of it did not appeal to me. The store card will still leave marks on your plate, but only very fine marks where you scrap it, and nothing at all that will mess up your image.<br /><br />I appreciate that the stamper itself is double sided and have used that to my advantage. Also it's worth mentioning that the rubber ends of the stamper can be pulled out, if you need them to for whatever reason. One time I put the rhinestones that I was going to use for a friends manicure in there, that way all I had to do was open up the stamper, it came in handy, so there's an idea. You wouldn't want to put anything too heavy in there of course as it would push the ends off.<br /><br />That's really all I say about this product other then some quick tips about doing stamping itself. I have found that it IS best to clean off the stamper between stamping even if its just collected dust, it will help. Then when you go to pick up an image make sure you do the process quick, paint, scrap, then roll your stamper over it with a firm steady hand. You have a small amount of time to position the image after you have it on the stamp, but don't wait too long as the image is so thin it will dry fast and probably mess up when you go to put it on. I've found if you figure out a way that is best for you, stamp that way every time, to reduce the time it takes. I was having trouble with stamping until I got down a system where I could do it quickly, that really helped. Also be careful not to press the hard edges of the stamper into your nail if it's still drying, as it will dent your polish. Once the image is on the nail make sure you're very careful about putting on a top coat as that can smudge your image.<br /><br />I hope this review helped. Happy Stamping!

If you do any sort of nail stamping, you need this double ended stamper and scraper. It's awesome, and it makes it easy to do stamps quickly since it's double sided. I do still recommend roughing up the edges with a nail-file before using. When I did this, the rubber stoppers both came out, but they popped right back in and have been relatively secure since.   930. Last year, I began stamping and decided at the start that I did not want to go the Konad branded route. I've not used the Konad plates, or the Konad stamping polish, I just didn't want to bother with Konad when there's plenty of other interchangeable brands that -don't- claim to be The Only One. I've been very happy with polishes and plates of tons of different brand, and I've never felt like I was missing anything because of that... but when it comes to the stamper, oh my. I bought myself a Konad stamper and thought of it as just standard, until I bought three stampers of various brands as gifts and realized that stampers are NOT all equal. The Konad stamper is FAR superior to all three other brands and if I had started with another brand stamper, I'd probably have given up after a day. The difference is in the rubber. The Konad stamper's rubber is soft and kind of &#34;sticky&#34;, yet firm and strong. It lifts images from any brand plates, any brand of thick polish, and it just... works. The other brands had awful hard plasticy rubber that wouldn't hold an image, and two of them had very rounded ends so it was impossible to pick up an image and then put it on your nail without rolling it around - so even if it picked up the image at all, which was rare, it just wasn't a smooth process and didn't have good results. The Konad stamper is the only stamper that has QUALITY rubber ends, and that makes all the difference. (As for the other piece in this package, I find old credit/gift cards easier to scrape image plates with- maybe it's the size and shape that makes it easier- but as long as it's firm, flat, and can scrape cleanly, you can't go wrong with a scraper tool)

This system took me a lot of getting used to, but it's so worth it.<br /><br />I found that using a nail buffer (not the more abrasive file, but y'know, a softer buff) on the new stamper did help take some of the waxy sheen off that made initial stamp transfers extra challenging, while also not destroying the equipment. Also found that an old credit card as a scraper worked consistently much better than the metal or plastic versions I got in these kits.<br /><br />I've also experimented with non-Konad polishes, and found good luck getting a solid stamp out of really any thick opaque polishes out there. Expensive polishes versus cheap-o versions really didn't make a difference, it was the thickness/opaqueness that won out. Deep matte polishes make especially great stamps.<br /><br />If you have the patience to potentially fail a lot and go through a lot of cleaning & re-work, you really will get the hang of it. I'm majorly cosmetically/beauty product challenged, but now get compliments from random folks & even the ladies at the nail salons for the fancy crap I've been able to pull off with this nifty little system.<br /><br />The dazzling possibilities become super exciting, and the fact that once you get this down, you can make pretty sweet insta-amaze-o designs on your nails in less than 10 minutes is handy and feels like winning/cheating at being fabulous.
